<div id="review_1020471144" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1020471144" />
    <a title="Lazaros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros"><img alt="Lazaros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578697302p2/22313662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1020471144?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lazaros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lazaros" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros">Lazaros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476740478" href="/book/show/17571724-one-tiny-lie">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">romantics</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1020471144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14009789325815923096"><i>
  <blockquote>“Life has a funny way of creating its own tests. It throws curve balls that make you do and think and feel things that are in direct conflict with what you had planned and don't allow you to operate in terms of black and white.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>This was better than I thought it would be. It started off nicely but as the story progressed I kind of lost interest and couldn't connect with the characters. But then that said connection was restored so in a way I enjoyed this a lot. In no way is it better than the</span>
  <span id="freeText14009789325815923096" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“Life has a funny way of creating its own tests. It throws curve balls that make you do and think and feel things that are in direct conflict with what you had planned and don't allow you to operate in terms of black and white.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />This was better than I thought it would be. It started off nicely but as the story progressed I kind of lost interest and couldn't connect with the characters. But then that said connection was restored so in a way I enjoyed this a lot. In no way is it better than the first novel in the series. The first one was really original and dark and it even had some twists. 'One Tiny Lie' was more colorful, although it was bleak too and went after the abuse theme.<br /><br />I liked Livie. I like how she's discovering herself after all these years of doing the mistake of identifying others' dreams as her own. With the help of Ashton, the hot rowing team dude, I think she finds what she wants to become and who she is, and while she is doing that, she falls in love. Ashton is probably the guy she should run from but she doesn't and it turns out it's a good thing. Livie and Kacey both have a magnet for fucked-up dudes, it seems. <br /><br />There's cheating in this book. Surprisingly, from Livie's side and not the other way around as most of you would assume. How, now, Livie manages from no boyfriends at all, ever, to reach the point where she has two, I don't even know. Yup, she is all grown up and you'll see how her sister and Dr. Stayner are trying to make her socialize but I think she ended up socializing too hard.<br /><br />Ashton is not the good guy. Or that's what it looks like at first. You'll have mixed feelings about him, until the view starts clearing up. That's it if you're not one for bad boys who hypothetically cheat on a hypothetical girlfriend every day. Don't judge someone by its wrapper.<br /><br />So, if you like a nice new-adult novel then go ahead and read this. At the end of the day you'll enjoy this. It's fun as it is dark and the characters are enjoyable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14009789325815923096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_593851419" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/593851419" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/593851419?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=great-premise-lacking-execution">great-premise-lacking-execution</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=mature">mature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=slice-of-life">slice-of-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=pretty-cover">pretty-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer593851419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3665289130838888736">For my review of "One Tiny Lie" - I'm not going to do much reflection and just cut to the chase, and hopefully without too many spoilers (though honestly, some of the turns of events are not that hard to figure out if you've read enough New Adult to see what elements are glorified). <br/><br/>Some might say that, considering what I rated the previous novel, this was a forgone reaction to a sequel of a novel I did not like, where I should've expected to see things coming along. But I have to refute that wi</span>
  <span id="freeText3665289130838888736" style="display:none">For my review of "One Tiny Lie" - I'm not going to do much reflection and just cut to the chase, and hopefully without too many spoilers (though honestly, some of the turns of events are not that hard to figure out if you've read enough New Adult to see what elements are glorified). <br /><br />Some might say that, considering what I rated the previous novel, this was a forgone reaction to a sequel of a novel I did not like, where I should've expected to see things coming along. But I have to refute that with some expansions.<br /><br />I'm splitting this review up into two sections - the first 60% and the last 40% of the novel. <br /><br />The first 60%, despite some qualms over things I saw - I was actually enjoying the novel. I would've probably given it a solid 3 stars for the portrayal of Livie's college experiences and the developing relationships, albeit some humorous, cliched anecdotes that are pretty typical of teen comedies, like the film "Can't Hardly Wait". It was probably the first time in a New Adult novel, I've seen, that a college environment - even with how loosely drawn it was of Princeton - was depicted with any kind of realistic terms for a Freshman trying to adjust and going through some absolutely mortifying situations (such as the drunken night one doesn't remember and ends up with a tattoo alongside a potential love interest being naked - maybe). I have to give it that much. Not only that, Livie's voice in the beginning is actually cool. She's funny, likable, even calls out her big sister Kacey (who was the MC to the previous novel) on things that are reminiscent of the maturity she had from the previous novel.<br /><br />I think anyone who reads the synopsis of this novel can tell that this is a story of Livie's respective fall from grace, from the "perfection" that exists in her mind and what everyone expects her to be to the reality of her coming to terms for what she really wants. That's a noble thing, I'm not knocking that at all and actually think that's a brilliant thing to cover. She's at the top of her game entering her freshman year, working hard to suit the expectations of her deceased father, who, Livie notes at the beginning of the novel, said "Make me proud." I think those of you who have read "Ten Tiny Breaths" know what happened with Kacey and Livie's family, so I'm not going to recap on that, but given the context of where this novel started off, I expected something of a light to dark rollercoaster, but treated with realism. <br /><br />I did have to suspend my disbelief on a few things, including the over the top therapist (Dr. Stayner, who actually struck me as more of a caricature representation of things that could've been shown with Livie coming to terms on her own. He was just as much of an intrusive presence in this novel as he was the former. He was one of the things that prevented me from enjoying the first part of the novel as much as I could've) and the fact that Livie's affections are torn between the usual good guy (Connor) versus the bad boy (Ashton). It's a typical set up for the love interest scenario, but I figured I could deal with that. Many love stories use the formula, it's a matter of how one uses them and if it comes across where we can root for the character and her decision, okay.<br /><br />Yet, the "One Tiny Lie" committed by Livie in measures ended up being more like 100 different lies balled into one with manipulations to match. While this could've been a chance for Livie to say "Okay, this is not who I am or who I wish to become, I've been lying to myself all this time and this is where it got me" and having her fall from grace and own up to the things she did wrong - this novel did no such thing. <br /><br /><br />It was, unfortunately, all about the chosen love story, which was probably a forgone conclusion even before the story really got off the ground.<br /><br />The last 40% of the novel (maybe even slightly before that point from clues in the set up) was an utter mess of melodrama. Not to mention familiar to cliches of New Adult (maybe even to contemp YA and adult romance) and some of the problematic things that others, including myself, have pointed out which contribute to the lack of diversity in this particular age group.<br /><br />Here's a question I pose to anyone who may come across this review, whether they may agree or disagree with the way that I view this novel: how is it right to vilify an entire group - a minority whether on racial, gender, sexual orientation, sexual preference or other distinctions - in order to basically say "This is not something that defines me or what I want"? One may say that slut and virgin shaming exist in real life and that this is fiction - okay, but where is the point when it becomes a reflection of reality or glorifying a problematic ideal in our society by putting it to be humored or an encompassing definition that's supposed to represent a norm? That the idea of being a virgin is "bad", while losing it and doing so at a certain stage in life is "good", when the reality is that people exist on variant scales and have different comfort zones and choices with that? How is it okay to say that cheating on a lover when it's *true love* is a positive thing while ignoring the repercussions it brings to all who may be affected by it? When is it a positive thing to say something like this:<br /><br /><i>"Connor is feeling more wrong by the minute. He looks perfect on the outside—smart, sweet, good-looking, charming. He does cute things like send me flowers and call me throughout the day to say hello. He's never pushed me into sex or anything aside from kissing, which, now that I think about it, is just plain weird for a college guy. Maybe he’s gay and I'm the perfect cover for his parents?Either way, it worked out well, because I’ve never had the urge to go farther with him. That in itself should have been a red flag for me."</i><br /><br />...and not recognize every single bit of what's wrong with it in real context, down to the groups it offends and the behaviors it vilifies? For justification, even for humor?<br /><br />I don't understand how that's right or acceptable. I really don't. I think there are ways to convey personal growth in a story without talking down the individual aspects that make us differ from one another. I think being able to recognize that would've made this a much stronger story that could resonate - with all audiences picking this up - without qualms, rather than marginalizing those who may fall in the affronted groups. It's a lesson any writer can take home with them at the end of the day.<br /><br />"One Tiny Lie" actually progresses to the point where, in the scheme of events, it does come across as one big release of conflict after conflict without a true coming to terms, in order for the professed "couple" (because it was never really a love triangle anyway) to bond. And it's complete with both a confession of difficult circumstances for both the hero and heroine that aren't really foreshadowed or given any due weight for the gravity that they have in themselves, but rather for the promotion of the formulaic conflict vehicle. Long story short, it's the same problems that peppered the last, and with a heroine who seemed to have a role that wasn't defined by that in the previous novel. Same script, different cast.<br /><br />In sum, I wish I could've liked this novel more, but I couldn't. I found it quite problematic and despite initial measures where it had my interest, it lost me - it dropped the ball for things it could've shown in better context, and I can't give it a recommendation. Maybe in time, I'll find a novel by the author that clicks with me, but not when it has this many problems contained within it.<br /><br />Overall score: 1/5 stars<br /><br />Note: I received this as an ARC from NetGalley, from the publisher Atria Books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3665289130838888736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1397934972" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1397934972" />
    <a title="Bj" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27341466-bj"><img alt="Bj" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396449537p2/27341466.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1397934972?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bj" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bj" href="/user/show/27341466-bj">Bj</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27341466-bj?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27341466-bj?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27341466-bj?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27341466-bj?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27341466-bj?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27341466-bj?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1397934972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17126418179572387371">5 "Longing for Freedom" Stars for both the story and the narration! <br/><br/>It is no secret that I have been a long-time fan of KA Tucker. This is the sixth book of hers I have either read or listened to, and I have loved each and every one of them. Perhaps the reason that I enjoy Ms. Tucker's writing so much is that while all her stories seem to have some level of romance intermixed with mystery/intrigue, they all defy a standard mold or formula. Instead each time you sit down to enjoy one of Ms. Tucke</span>
  <span id="freeText17126418179572387371" style="display:none">5 "Longing for Freedom" Stars for both the story and the narration! <br /><br />It is no secret that I have been a long-time fan of KA Tucker. This is the sixth book of hers I have either read or listened to, and I have loved each and every one of them. Perhaps the reason that I enjoy Ms. Tucker's writing so much is that while all her stories seem to have some level of romance intermixed with mystery/intrigue, they all defy a standard mold or formula. Instead each time you sit down to enjoy one of Ms. Tucker's creations, you know that you will be treated to a fresh and entertaining, emotionally complex story that defies convention but which you are sure to feel down deep in your heart. One Tiny Lie is no different. This story made me laugh, cry and swoon, all at different points throughout, but, no matter what, always kept me glued to my earbuds! <br /><br />For those of you who are wondering whether One Tiny Lie can be read as a stand-alone, the answer is yes, as I listened to it as a stand-alone! Although this is book 2 in the Ten Tiny Breaths Series--and does involve a character that plays a prominent role in book 1 (Livie, who is the little sister of the heroine in Book 1, is the heroine of book 2)--I had no trouble following the story line as the entire romance arc, and a sufficient amount of the heroine's tragic past is explained in One Tiny Lie. <br /><br />Having been the strong, dependable sister following her parents' tragic death in a car accident, notwithstanding that she was the younger sister, Livie has always remained faithful to her promise to her father that she would become a pediatric oncologist. Now that she is finally starting college at her parents' old alma mater, Princeton, she is getting closer to realizing her dreams. Livie's sister however, as well as her psychologist, seem concerned that Livie is bound for a breakdown if she continues down her current pressure laden path. So part of their plan, which is happily aided by Livie's, party girl roommate, is to get Livie to let her hair down, relax, party, as well as, finally lose her virginity. Livie, however, is not so sure she needs the distraction, or needs to change her goals, until she meets exactly the wrong boy, Ashton (the captain of the rowing team) during a wild night at a toga party. Moreover, when the perfect, marriage material, long-term plan worthy guy (Connor) does ask her out, and begins to show interest in her, Livie is left to ponder just what exactly she really wants out of life. <br /><br />Elizabeth Louise delivers a fantastic performance in One Tiny Lie. She perfectly nails not just Livie's character, but each and every one of the numerous other characters that play a part in One Tiny Lie. She is even tested with accents and ages, as Connor has a mild Irish brogue, his father a stronger one and there are even several children in the story; and Ms. Louise performs believable, authentic characterizations on all fronts.<br /><br />Moreover, my favorite part of Ms. Louise's performance is that she is a master at conveying emotion. This talent is incredibly useful in an emotion rich story like One Tiny Lie. The end result is that Ms. Louise not just reads us this touching story, but she actually manages to bring it to life!<br /><br />If you have not yet had a chance to experience One Tiny Lie, then I highly recommend that you do. Moreover, if you're an audiobook fan, then Ms. Louise's talented narration makes this a great story to experience in audio format.<br /><br />Source: Review copy provided in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17126418179572387371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_546166826" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/546166826" />
    <a title="Paula " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2879703-paula"><img alt="Paula " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536687412p2/2879703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/546166826?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula " href="/user/show/2879703-paula">Paula </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2879703-paula?shelf=fantabulous-favorites">fantabulous-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2879703-paula?shelf=new-adult-romance">new-adult-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer546166826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11503961246360262974"><br/>I'm feeling nostalgic so I read this one again...just as awesome the second time around. <br/><br/>****************************************<br/><br/>Livie Cleary, Kacey’s little sister from <i>Ten Tiny Breaths</i>, is now all grown up in <i>One Tiny Lie</i>.. With a flawless academic career, she is now attending Princeton University--her ultimate goal being medical school. Livie may be level headed, responsible, cautious, calm, and trustworthy, but she’s never actually <i>lived her life</i>. Livie has always been the strong and stable </span>
  <span id="freeText11503961246360262974" style="display:none"><br />I'm feeling nostalgic so I read this one again...just as awesome the second time around. <br /><br />****************************************<br /><br />Livie Cleary, Kacey’s little sister from <i>Ten Tiny Breaths</i>, is now all grown up in <i>One Tiny Lie</i>.. With a flawless academic career, she is now attending Princeton University--her ultimate goal being medical school. Livie may be level headed, responsible, cautious, calm, and trustworthy, but she’s never actually <i>lived her life</i>. Livie has always been the strong and stable sister. She’s been there for Kacey through thick and thin after Kacey lost her way after their parent’s died in a terrible car accident. This is why Kacey has decided to step in and help her little sister, who has built this life that oozes perfection. Kacey has enlisted Dr. Stayner, her therapist, to help break through Livie’s shell and find out what’s underneath before she completely loses herself in a life that may not be meant for her. Kacey and Dr. Stayner think it’s time for Livie to spread her wings, make mistakes, be spontaneous… live HER life, not the life she thinks would make her father proud. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“You are one of the kindest souls I’ve ever met, Livie. You respond to human heartache so acutely. It’s like you absorb other’s pain. Despite your extreme shyness, you will do just about anything not to fail. It’s time to find out who you really are.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Her first night at Princeton, Livie goes to a college toga party with Kacey and Reagan, Livie’s very wild and outgoing new roommate. Kacey’s mission: get Livie drunk, make sure she has fun, and ‘liberate Livie’s libido.’ As the Jell-O shots continue to go down, Livie starts to loosen up and have a good time. Just as she drops another one in her mouth, a super sexy guy not only steals her shot, but steals her first kiss. And then Livie punches him. It was lust at first punch. <br /><br />The next morning, after a <i>long night</i> of partying, Livie wakes up hung over, in only her panties, tattooed, with no memory of the night before, and… with a very naked Ashton Henley, aka the Jell-O thief, in her dorm room. And, unfortunately, the awkward encounter is not the last she sees of Ashton. From this moment on, Livie’s whole life begins to unravel as she spirals down a rabbit hole of deception, betrayal, confusion, cheating, bad grades, love, and heartache. <br /><br />Oh, Ashton – such a tortured hero. He’s known for being captain of the Princeton Heavyweight rowing team, sexiest man on campus, arrogant, and being a bit of a man whore. Not so surprisingly, I fell in lust with him from the moment he stole Livie’s Jell-O shot. But… he has a girlfriend… and he cheats on her. Wait. Don’t judge until you meet Ashton. I’m not condoning the cheating. However, I quickly got over my reservations once I got to know him. Ashton has some deep, dark issues that shape who he is as a person. His secrets are gut-wrenching and they force him to be someone that he never chose to be. He’s hurting and just wants to forget it all. <br /><br />When Livie finds out Ashton cheats on his girl with her and other girls, she’s stunned and hurt, so she goes to great lengths to avoid Ashton. There is no way she wants to be associated with someone like that. Though it’s hard to avoid Ashton when he’s everywhere, charming his way into her life while also continuing to push her away. The more she’s around him, the more she’s drawn to him. She can’t stop thinking about him. But Ashton is not the kind of guy her parent’s would approve of. So Livie starts dating Connor, Ashton’s best friend. He’s respectable, kind, and safe. Her parents would like him so that makes him perfect for Livie except… she doesn’t have the same kind of emotional, intense chemistry with Connor that she has with Ashton. Connor is not the guy that makes her stomach flutter and her toes curl when he kisses her. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Because you're not a one-night girl, Irish." Leaning in to place a kiss on my jawline, he whispers, "You're my forever girl."</b>
</i><br /><br />To say the situation between Connor, Ashton, and Livie is complicated is quite the understatement. Livie has this huge heart and feels obligated to stay with Connor. She’s torn between following along her life plan and following her heart. Yet the more she gets to know the true Ashton, the harder she falls for him. What’s a girl to do? Stay with the guy who is safe or the bad boy she feels connected to? Livie is so confused. Especially since Ashton and Livie obviously belong together, but he would push and pull Livie in two different directions. He wants her. He wants her not. There were moments my heart didn’t know if it could take any more rejection from Ashton. But then he would leave a sweet note or open up to Livie. These things would make me shiver and tingle in a good way. What it boils down to – I wanted nothing more than for these two to find a way to be together. <br /><br />All of the secondary characters are fun and charismatic. I love seeing the roles reverse between Livie and Kacey. This time, Kacey plays a large role in helping Livie find herself. It was good to see Kacey and Trent happy and settled in their lives. They’ve both come so far since their story in Ten Tiny Breaths. Then there is Livie’s roommate, Reagan. She’s so spunky and fun-loving and such a great friend to Livie. Part of me wishes she was getting her own book. And then there was the quirky Dr. Stayner – such an interesting character who plays an essential role in this story. His unusual therapy methods contributed to helping Livie discover her inner self. <br /><br /><i>One Tiny Lie</i> is a compelling story that manages to evoke a gamut of emotions from me. I felt like my heart strings were being stretched so thin at times that I kept wondering if these two will ever figure things out before they broke. This is one of those stories where I think the reader is going to either love or hate it. Any story that involves cheating is not an easy read. You will be frustrated with Livie and Ashton’s mistakes. They make a ton of mistakes that hurt people in the process. There were times when I wanted to scream and hug them at the same time. I was an emotional wreck, I tell you. And my anxiety was on the fritz. But there is a lesson to learn here that I think most young adults must experience. Life is messy and it’s all part of living and learning. When you entwine all the great humor, sadness, happiness, wonderful characters, emotional turmoil, drama, and romance – you have a remarkable story that I fell madly in love with. <br /><br />Rating: A<br />Heat: Warm<br /><br /><br />-- <i>A <a href="http://romanticbookaffairs.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Romantic Book Affairs</a> Review</i><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Find us on <a href="https://twitter.com/rombookaffairs" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> and <a href="http://facebook.com/rombookaffairs" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> too!</i>
</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17786670907242834474">This gave me definite <b>Thoughtless</b> vibes.<br/><br/>I don't usually seek out cheating books, but I have found that I find them incredibly addicting! I was fighting for these two so hard. I couldn't wait to unveil all the reasons that Ashton kept Livie at a distance. But I absolutely loved their attraction to each other, their obsession for each other. <br/><br/>One thing that I hope is a common theme to this series: Dr. Stayner. Although his plot in this book isn't very plausible, I found it awesome all the same. On </span>
  <span id="freeText17786670907242834474" style="display:none">This gave me definite <b>Thoughtless</b> vibes.<br /><br />I don't usually seek out cheating books, but I have found that I find them incredibly addicting! But I absolutely loved their attraction to each other, their obsession for each other. <br /><br />One thing that I hope is a common theme to this series: Dr. Stayner. Although his plot in this book isn't very plausible, I found it awesome all the same. On to <b>Four Seconds to Lose.</b></span>

</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/qVGfeUKuUIkbCx+doF5stp1AfachV+TblQDjlJdpX3DXjj2l3z9MBJdca0es+F1di0Y3sCOwOrX7YAhS4dllQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Co121Yt5U+ILSzPOpuE8RkqoDmyIHPKYKnS4xhDupJg3dghe+Q8XkD16bh3O06SB5vAXRNQXbeGTzTtpCTRkcA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText11369269946021072391" style="display:none">K.A. Tucker writes captivating stories with an edge.<br /><br />She is the internationally bestselling author of the Ten Tiny Breaths and Burying Water series, He Will Be My Ruin, Until It Fades, Keep Her Safe, The Simple Wild, Be the Girl, and Say You Still Love Me. Her books have been featured in national publications including USA Today, Globe &amp; Mail, Suspense Magazine, Publisher's Weekly, Oprah Mag, and First for Women. She has been nominated for the Goodreads Choice Award for Best Romance 2013 for TEN TINY BREATHS and Best Romance 2018 for THE SIMPLE WILD. KEEP HER SAFE made Suspense Magazine's Best of 2018 list for Romantic Suspense.<br /><br />K.A.
